<div class="vector-body" id="bodyContent">

<div class="mw-body-content mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Roman civilization from the 8th century BCE to the 5th century CE</div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1033289096">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}</style><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">This article is about the <a href="/wiki/History_of_Rome" title="History of Rome">history of Roman civilisation</a> in <a href="/wiki/Ancient_history" title="Ancient history">antiquity</a>. For the history of the city of Rome, see <a href="/wiki/Rome" title="Rome">Rome</a>. For other uses, see <a class="mw-disambig" href="/wiki/Ancient_Rome_(disambiguation)" title="Ancient Rome (disambiguation)">Ancient Rome (disambiguation)</a>.</div>

<div class="hlist hlist-separated" style="text-align:center;font-weight:normal;">
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Outline_of_political_science#Politics_by_region" title="Outline of political science">Other countries</a></li></ul>
</div></td></tr><tr><td class="sidebar-navbar" style="text-align:center;"><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1063604349">.mw-parser-output .navbar{display:inline;font-size:88%;font-weight:normal}.mw-parser-output .navbar-collapse{float:left;text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .navbar-boxtext{word-spacing:0}.mw-parser-output .navbar ul{display:inline-block;white-space:nowrap;line-height:inherit}.mw-parser-output .navbar-brackets::before{margin-right:-0.125em;content:"[ "}.mw-parser-output .navbar-brackets::after{margin-left:-0.125em;content:" ]"}.mw-parser-output .navbar li{word-spacing:-0.125em}.mw-parser-output .navbar a>span,.mw-parser-output .navbar a>abbr{text-decoration:inherit}.mw-parser-output .navbar-mini abbr{font-variant:small-caps;border-bottom:none;text-decoration:none;cursor:inherit}.mw-parser-output .navbar-ct-full{font-size:114%;margin:0 7em}.mw-parser-output .navbar-ct-mini{font-size:114%;margin:0 4em}</style><div class="navbar plainlinks hlist navbar-mini"><ul><li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:Politics_of_ancient_Rome" title="Template:Politics of ancient Rome"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Politics_of_ancient_Rome" title="Template talk:Politics of ancient Rome"><abbr title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Politics_of_ancient_Rome&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li></ul></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>In modern <a href="/wiki/Historiography" title="Historiography">historiography</a>, <b>ancient Rome</b> refers to <a href="/wiki/Roman_people" title="Roman people">Roman</a> civilization from the founding of the city of <a href="/wiki/Rome" title="Rome">Rome</a> in the 8th century BC to the collapse of the <a href="/wiki/Western_Roman_Empire" title="Western Roman Empire">Western Roman Empire</a> in the 5th century AD. It encompasses the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Kingdom" title="Roman Kingdom">Roman Kingdom</a> (753–509 BC), <a href="/wiki/Roman_Republic" title="Roman Republic">Roman Republic</a> (509–27 BC) and <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Roman Empire</a> (27 BC–476 AD) until the fall of the western empire.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup>
</p><p>Ancient Rome began as an <a href="/wiki/Italic_peoples" title="Italic peoples">Italic</a> settlement, traditionally dated to 753 BC, beside the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/River_Tiber" title="River Tiber">River Tiber</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Italy" title="Roman Italy">Italian Peninsula</a>. The settlement grew into the city and polity of Rome, and came to control its neighbours through a combination of treaties and military strength. It eventually dominated the Italian peninsula, and acquired an Empire that took in much of Europe and the lands and peoples surrounding the Mediterranean Sea. It was among the <a href="/wiki/List_of_largest_empires" title="List of largest empires">largest empires</a> in the ancient world, with an estimated 50 to 90 million inhabitants, roughly 20% of the world's population at the time. It covered around 5 million square kilometres (1.9 million square miles) at its height in AD 117.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-:0-3">[3]</a></sup>
</p><p>The Roman state evolved from an <a href="/wiki/Roman_Kingdom" title="Roman Kingdom">elective monarchy</a> to a <a href="/wiki/Direct_democracy" title="Direct democracy">democratic</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Classical_republic" title="Classical republic">classical republic</a> and then to an increasingly <a href="/wiki/Autocracy" title="Autocracy">autocratic</a> <a href="/wiki/Elective_monarchy" title="Elective monarchy">semi-elective</a> <a href="/wiki/Military_dictatorship" title="Military dictatorship">military dictatorship</a> during the Empire. Through conquest, <a href="/wiki/Cultural_assimilation" title="Cultural assimilation">cultural</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Language_shift" title="Language shift">linguistic</a> <a href="/wiki/Romanization_(cultural)" title="Romanization (cultural)">assimilation</a>, at its height it controlled the <a href="/wiki/North_Africa_during_Antiquity" title="North Africa during Antiquity">North African</a> coast, <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egypt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Southern_Europe" title="Southern Europe">Southern Europe</a>, and most of <a href="/wiki/Western_Europe" title="Western Europe">Western Europe</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Balkans" title="Balkans">Balkans</a>, <a href="/wiki/Crimea" title="Crimea">Crimea</a> and much of the <a href="/wiki/Middle_East" title="Middle East">Middle East</a>, including <a href="/wiki/Anatolia" title="Anatolia">Anatolia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Levant" title="Levant">Levant</a> and parts of <a href="/wiki/Mesopotamia" title="Mesopotamia">Mesopotamia</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arabia" title="Arabia">Arabia</a>. It is often grouped into <a href="/wiki/Classical_antiquity" title="Classical antiquity">classical antiquity</a> together with <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Greece" title="Ancient Greece">ancient Greece</a>, and their similar cultures and societies are known as the <a href="/wiki/Greco-Roman_world" title="Greco-Roman world">Greco-Roman world</a>.
</p><p>Ancient Roman civilisation has contributed to modern language, religion, society, technology, law, politics, government, warfare, art, literature, architecture and engineering. Rome professionalised and expanded its military and created a system of government called <i><a href="/wiki/Res_publica" title="Res publica">res publica</a></i>, the inspiration for modern <a href="/wiki/Republic" title="Republic">republics</a> such as the United States and France.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup> It achieved impressive <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_technology" title="Roman technology">technological</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Roman_architecture" title="Ancient Roman architecture">architectural</a> feats, such as the empire-wide construction of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_aqueducts" title="Roman aqueducts">aqueducts</a> and <a href="/wiki/Roman_roads" title="Roman roads">roads</a>, as well as more grandiose monuments and facilities.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Punic_Wars" title="Punic Wars">Punic Wars</a> with <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Carthage" title="Ancient Carthage">Carthage</a> gave Rome supremacy in the Mediterranean. The Roman Empire emerged with the <a href="/wiki/Principate" title="Principate">principate</a> of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Augustus_Caesar" title="Augustus Caesar">Augustus</a> (from 27 BC); Rome's imperial domain now extended from the Atlantic to <a href="/wiki/Arabia_Petraea" title="Arabia Petraea">Arabia</a> and from the mouth of the <a href="/wiki/Rhine" title="Rhine">Rhine</a> to North Africa. In 92 AD, Rome came up against the resurgent <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Persian_Empire" title="Persian Empire">Persian Empire</a> and became involved in history's longest-running conflict, the <a href="/wiki/Roman%E2%80%93Persian_Wars" title="Roman–Persian Wars">Roman–Persian Wars</a>, which would have lasting effects on both empires. Under <a href="/wiki/Trajan" title="Trajan">Trajan</a>, Rome's empire reached its territorial peak, encompassing the entire <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_Basin" title="Mediterranean Basin">Mediterranean Basin</a>, the southern margins of the <a href="/wiki/North_Sea" title="North Sea">North Sea</a>, and the shores of the <a href="/wiki/Red_Sea" title="Red Sea">Red</a> and <a href="/wiki/Caspian_Sea" title="Caspian Sea">Caspian</a> Seas. Republican <a href="/wiki/Mos_maiorum" title="Mos maiorum">mores and traditions</a> started to decline during the imperial period, with civil wars becoming a common prelude to the rise of a new emperor.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> Splinter states, such as the <a href="/wiki/Palmyrene_Empire" title="Palmyrene Empire">Palmyrene Empire</a>, would temporarily divide the Empire during the <a href="/wiki/Crisis_of_the_Third_Century" title="Crisis of the Third Century">crisis of the 3rd century</a> before some stability was restored in the <a href="/wiki/Tetrarchy" title="Tetrarchy">Tetrarchy</a> phase of imperial rule.
</p><p>Plagued by internal instability and <a href="/wiki/Migration_Period" title="Migration Period">attacked</a> by various migrating peoples, the western part of the empire <a href="/wiki/Fall_of_the_Western_Roman_Empire" title="Fall of the Western Roman Empire">broke up</a> into independent <a href="/wiki/Barbarian_kingdoms" title="Barbarian kingdoms">barbarian kingdoms</a> in the 5th century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[a]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Empire" title="Byzantine Empire">eastern part of the empire</a> remained a power through the Middle Ages until its <a href="/wiki/Fall_of_Constantinople" title="Fall of Constantinople">fall</a> in 1453 AD.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[b]</a></sup>
</p>

<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-46"><a href="#Technology"><span class="tocnumber">10</span> <span class="toctext">Technology</span></a></li>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_Italy_and_the_founding_of_Rome">Early Italy and the founding of Rome</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ancient_Rome&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Early Italy and the founding of Rome">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Founding_of_Rome" title="Founding of Rome">Founding of Rome</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Origini_di_roma_in_narrazione_continua,_da_pompei_V_4,_13,_s.n..JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2688" data-file-width="2208" decoding="async" height="268" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Origini_di_roma_in_narrazione_continua%2C_da_pompei_V_4%2C_13%2C_s.n..JPG/220px-Origini_di_roma_in_narrazione_continua%2C_da_pompei_V_4%2C_13%2C_s.n..JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Origini_di_roma_in_narrazione_continua%2C_da_pompei_V_4%2C_13%2C_s.n..JPG/330px-Origini_di_roma_in_narrazione_continua%2C_da_pompei_V_4%2C_13%2C_s.n..JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Origini_di_roma_in_narrazione_continua%2C_da_pompei_V_4%2C_13%2C_s.n..JPG/440px-Origini_di_roma_in_narrazione_continua%2C_da_pompei_V_4%2C_13%2C_s.n..JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Origini_di_roma_in_narrazione_continua,_da_pompei_V_4,_13,_s.n..JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A fresco from <a href="/wiki/Pompeii" title="Pompeii">Pompeii</a> depicting the foundation of Rome. <a href="/wiki/Sol_(Roman_mythology)" title="Sol (Roman mythology)">Sol</a> riding in his chariot; <a href="/wiki/Mars_(mythology)" title="Mars (mythology)">Mars</a> descending from the sky to <a href="/wiki/Rhea_Silvia" title="Rhea Silvia">Rhea Silvia</a> lying in the grass; <a href="/wiki/Mercury_(mythology)" title="Mercury (mythology)">Mercury</a> shows to <a href="/wiki/Venus_(mythology)" title="Venus (mythology)">Venus</a> the she-wolf suckling the twins; in the lower corners of the picture: river-god <a href="/wiki/Tiberinus_(god)" title="Tiberinus (god)">Tiberinus</a> and water-goddess <a href="/wiki/Juturna" title="Juturna">Juturna</a>. 35-45 CE.</div></div></div>
<p>Agriculture appeared in Italy <abbr title="circa">c.</abbr><span style="white-space:nowrap;"> 4000 BC</span>, with <a href="/wiki/Chalcolithic" title="Chalcolithic">copper</a> tools appearing <abbr title="circa">c.</abbr><span style="white-space:nowrap;"> 2000 BC</span> followed by the Bronze Age through to end of the second millenium BC.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBoatwright20126_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBoatwright20126-9">[7]</a></sup> Cities started developing in the 9th century BC with the <a href="/wiki/Villanovan_culture" title="Villanovan culture">Villanovan culture</a> in Etruria. A culture specific to Latium – called the <a href="/wiki/Latial_culture" title="Latial culture">Latial culture</a> – appears in the archaeological record <abbr title="circa">c.</abbr><span style="white-space:nowrap;"> 1000 BC</span>, which was related to the larger Villanovans.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBoatwright20127–8_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBoatwright20127–8-10">[8]</a></sup> From the middle of the 8th century to the 5th century BC, city-states were created became the dominant form of political organisation in Italy;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBoatwright20129_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBoatwright20129-11">[9]</a></sup> they also started to build organised cityscapes and religious cult centres.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBoatwright201214_et_seq_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBoatwright201214_et_seq-12">[10]</a></sup> By the 7th century BC, large organised city-states had emerged in Etruria; their influence over Italy was such that later Roman writers believed many of their core traditions were of <a href="/wiki/Etruscan_civilization" title="Etruscan civilization">Etruscan</a> origin.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBoatwright201227_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBoatwright201227-13">[11]</a></sup>
</p><p>Archaeological evidence of settlement around Rome starts to emerge <abbr title="circa">c.</abbr><span style="white-space:nowrap;"> 1000 BC</span>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBoatwright2012519_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBoatwright2012519-14">[12]</a></sup> Large-scale organisation appears only <abbr title="circa">c.</abbr><span style="white-space:nowrap;"> 800 BC</span>, with the first graves in the <a href="/wiki/Esquiline_Hill" title="Esquiline Hill">Esquiline Hill</a>'s necropolis, along with discover of a clay and timber wall on the bottom of the <a href="/wiki/Palatine_Hill" title="Palatine Hill">Palatine Hill</a> dating to the middle of the 8th century BC. Starting from <abbr title="circa">c.</abbr><span style="white-space:nowrap;"> 650 BC</span>, the Romans started to drain the valley between the <a href="/wiki/Capitoline_Hill" title="Capitoline Hill">Capitoline</a> and Palatine Hills, where today sits the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Forum" title="Roman Forum">Roman Forum</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBoatwright201229_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBoatwright201229-15">[13]</a></sup> By the sixth century, the Romans were constructing the <a href="/wiki/Temple_of_Jupiter_Optimus_Maximus" title="Temple of Jupiter Optimus Maximus">Temple of Jupiter Optimus Maximus</a> on the Capitoline and expanding to the <a href="/wiki/Forum_Boarium" title="Forum Boarium">Forum Boarium</a> located between the Capitoline and <a href="/wiki/Aventine_Hill" title="Aventine Hill">Aventine Hills</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBoatwright201231_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBoatwright201231-16">[14]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Capitoline_she-wolf_Musei_Capitolini_MC1181.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2400" data-file-width="3200" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Capitoline_she-wolf_Musei_Capitolini_MC1181.jpg/220px-Capitoline_she-wolf_Musei_Capitolini_MC1181.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Capitoline_she-wolf_Musei_Capitolini_MC1181.jpg/330px-Capitoline_she-wolf_Musei_Capitolini_MC1181.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Capitoline_she-wolf_Musei_Capitolini_MC1181.jpg/440px-Capitoline_she-wolf_Musei_Capitolini_MC1181.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Capitoline_she-wolf_Musei_Capitolini_MC1181.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>According to legend, <a href="/wiki/Founding_of_Rome" title="Founding of Rome">Rome was founded</a> in 753 BC by <a href="/wiki/Romulus_and_Remus" title="Romulus and Remus">Romulus and Remus</a>, who were raised by a she-wolf.</div></div></div>
<p>The Romans themselves had a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Founding_myth" title="Founding myth">founding myth</a>. They attributed their city to a dispute in the ruling family of the mythical city of <a href="/wiki/Alba_Longa" title="Alba Longa">Alba Longa</a>: when its king was deposed, one of its princesses was forced to become a <a href="/wiki/Vestal_Virgin" title="Vestal Virgin">virgin priestess</a> of <a href="/wiki/Vesta_(mythology)" title="Vesta (mythology)">Vesta</a> but was impregnated by Mars and bore two twins, <a href="/wiki/Romulus_and_Remus" title="Romulus and Remus">Romulus and Remus</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBoatwright201231–32_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBoatwright201231–32-17">[15]</a></sup> The sons, sentenced to death, were rescued first by a she-wolf and thence by farmers, before returning to restore the deposed Alban king and founding a city where they had been rescued. After a dispute, Romulus killed Remus and became the city's sole founder. The story dates at least to the third century, and the later Roman antiquarian <a href="/wiki/Marcus_Terentius_Varro" title="Marcus Terentius Varro">Marcus Terentius Varro</a> placed the city's foundation to the well-known date 753 BC.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBoatwright201232_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBoatwright201232-18">[16]</a></sup>
</p><p>Another legend, recorded by Greek historian <a href="/wiki/Dionysius_of_Halicarnassus" title="Dionysius of Halicarnassus">Dionysius of Halicarnassus</a>, says that Prince Aeneas led a group of Trojans on a sea voyage to found a new Troy, since the original was destroyed at the end of the <a href="/wiki/Trojan_War" title="Trojan War">Trojan War</a>. After a long time in rough seas, they landed on the banks of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tiber_River" title="Tiber River">Tiber River</a>. Not long after they landed, the men wanted to take to the sea again, but the women who were traveling with them did not want to leave. One woman, named Roma, suggested that the women burn the ships out at sea to prevent their leaving. At first, the men were angry with Roma, but they soon realized that they were in the ideal place to settle. They named the settlement after the woman who torched their ships.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[17]</a></sup>
</p><p>The Roman poet <a href="/wiki/Virgil" title="Virgil">Virgil</a> recounted this legend in his classical epic poem the <i><a href="/wiki/Aeneid" title="Aeneid">Aeneid</a></i>, where the Trojan prince <a href="/wiki/Aeneas" title="Aeneas">Aeneas</a> is destined by the gods to found a new Troy. In the epic, the women also refuse to go back to the sea, but they were not left on the Tiber. After reaching Italy, Aeneas, who wanted to marry <a href="/wiki/Lavinia" title="Lavinia">Lavinia</a>, was forced to wage war with her former suitor, <a href="/wiki/Turnus" title="Turnus">Turnus</a>. According to the poem, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Latin_kings_of_Alba_Longa" title="Latin kings of Alba Longa">Alban kings</a> were descended from Aeneas, and thus Romulus, the founder of Rome, was his descendant.
</p>
<div class="timeline-wrapper"><map name="timeline_qdstb41jlnydtdzsucjg9p6mr5mjd3z"><area alt="Byzantine Empire" coords="528,49,641,70" href="/wiki/Byzantine_Empire" shape="rect" title="Byzantine Empire"/><area alt="Roman Empire" coords="318,29,388,50" href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" shape="rect" title="Roman Empire"/><area alt="Roman Republic" coords="188,29,269,50" href="/wiki/Roman_Republic" shape="rect" title="Roman Republic"/><area alt="Roman Kingdom" coords="78,29,153,50" href="/wiki/Roman_Kingdom" shape="rect" title="Roman Kingdom"/><area alt="Western Roman Empire" coords="375,9,488,30" href="/wiki/Western_Roman_Empire" shape="rect" title="Western Roman Empire"/></map><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/timeline/qdstb41jlnydtdzsucjg9p6mr5mjd3z.png" usemap="#timeline_qdstb41jlnydtdzsucjg9p6mr5mjd3z"/></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Kingdom">Kingdom</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ancient_Rome&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Kingdom">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Roman_Kingdom" title="Roman Kingdom">Roman Kingdom</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Danseurs_et_musiciens,_tombe_des_l%C3%A9opards.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1603" data-file-width="2892" decoding="async" height="122" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Danseurs_et_musiciens%2C_tombe_des_l%C3%A9opards.jpg/220px-Danseurs_et_musiciens%2C_tombe_des_l%C3%A9opards.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Danseurs_et_musiciens%2C_tombe_des_l%C3%A9opards.jpg/330px-Danseurs_et_musiciens%2C_tombe_des_l%C3%A9opards.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Danseurs_et_musiciens%2C_tombe_des_l%C3%A9opards.jpg/440px-Danseurs_et_musiciens%2C_tombe_des_l%C3%A9opards.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Danseurs_et_musiciens,_tombe_des_l%C3%A9opards.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Etruscan_Civilization" title="Etruscan Civilization">Etruscan</a> <a href="/wiki/Etruscan_art" title="Etruscan art">painting</a>; dancer and musicians, <a href="/wiki/Tomb_of_the_Leopards" title="Tomb of the Leopards">Tomb of the Leopards</a>, in Tarquinia, Italy.</div></div></div>
<p>Literary and archaeological evidence is clear on there having been kings in Rome, attested in fragmentary 6th century BC texts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[18]</a></sup> Long after the abolition of the Roman monarchy, a vestigial <i>rex sacrorum</i> was retained to exercise the monarch's former priestly functions. The Romans believed that their monarchy was elective, with seven legendary kings who were largely unrelated by blood.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBoatwright201236_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBoatwright201236-21">[19]</a></sup>
</p><p>Evidence of Roman expansion is clear in the sixth century BC; by its end, Rome controlled a territory of some 300 square miles with a population perhaps as high as 35,000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBoatwright201236_21-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBoatwright201236-21">[19]</a></sup> A palace, the <a href="/wiki/Regia" title="Regia">Regia</a>, was constructed <abbr title="circa">c.</abbr><span style="white-space:nowrap;"> 625 BC</span>;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBoatwright201236_21-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBoatwright201236-21">[19]</a></sup> the Romans attributed the creation of their first popular organisations and the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Senate" title="Roman Senate">Senate</a> to the regal period as well.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBoatwright201237_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBoatwright201237-22">[20]</a></sup> Rome also started to extend its control over its Latin neighbours. While later Roman stories like the <i><a href="/wiki/Aeneid" title="Aeneid">Aeneid</a></i> asserted that all Latins descended from the titular character <a href="/wiki/Aeneas" title="Aeneas">Aeneas</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBoatwright201239_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBoatwright201239-23">[21]</a></sup> a common culture is attested to archaeologically.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBoatwright201240_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBoatwright201240-24">[22]</a></sup> Attested to reciprocal rights of marriage and citizenship between Latin cities – the <span title="Latin-language text"><i lang="la"><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jus_Latii" title="Jus Latii">Jus Latii</a></i></span> – along with shared religious festivals, further indicate a shared culture. By the end of the 6th century, most of this area had become dominated by the Romans.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBoatwright201242_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBoatwright201242-25">[23]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Republic">Republic</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ancient_Rome&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Republic">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Roman_Republic" title="Roman Republic">Roman Republic</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Capitoline_Brutus_Musei_Capitolini_MC1183_02.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1950" data-file-width="1300" decoding="async" height="255" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Capitoline_Brutus_Musei_Capitolini_MC1183_02.jpg/170px-Capitoline_Brutus_Musei_Capitolini_MC1183_02.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Capitoline_Brutus_Musei_Capitolini_MC1183_02.jpg/255px-Capitoline_Brutus_Musei_Capitolini_MC1183_02.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Capitoline_Brutus_Musei_Capitolini_MC1183_02.jpg/340px-Capitoline_Brutus_Musei_Capitolini_MC1183_02.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Capitoline_Brutus_Musei_Capitolini_MC1183_02.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Capitoline_Brutus" title="Capitoline Brutus">This bust</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Capitoline_Museums" title="Capitoline Museums">Capitoline Museums</a> is traditionally identified as a portrait of <a href="/wiki/Lucius_Junius_Brutus" title="Lucius Junius Brutus">Lucius Junius Brutus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Roman_sculpture" title="Roman sculpture">Roman</a> <a href="/wiki/Bronze_sculpture" title="Bronze sculpture">bronze sculpture</a>, 4th to late 3rd centuries BC.</div></div></div>
<p>By the end of the sixth century, Rome and many of its Italian neighbours entered a period of turbulence. Archaeological evidence implies some degree of large-scale warfare; many neighbouring cities in Etruria also shifted to non-monarchical institutions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBoatwright201243_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBoatwright201243-26">[24]</a></sup> While Roman traditions believed that the <a href="/wiki/Overthrow_of_the_Roman_monarchy" title="Overthrow of the Roman monarchy">overthrow of the Roman monarchy</a> inaugurated a new and concrete republic, it is implausible the transition could have been so sharp.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBoatwright201244_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBoatwright201244-27">[25]</a></sup> The Romans believed that from the birth of the republic, they established a two-man magistracy taking over the king's powers: the <a href="/wiki/Roman_consul" title="Roman consul">consulship</a>. These magistrates had short one-year terms and held office with colleagues that could check each others actions. The prevalance in both Rome and other cities at this time of replacing monarchs with elected officials suggests that Italian aristocratic families "never bec[a]me fully reconciled to the rule of one man".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBoatwright201244_27-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBoatwright201244-27">[25]</a></sup> Through the following centuries, the Romans experimented with different offices and constitutional regimes before settling on the two consuls in the fourth century BC.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBoatwright201244_27-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBoatwright201244-27">[25]</a></sup>
</p><p>According to tradition and later writers such as <a href="/wiki/Livy" title="Livy">Livy</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Republic" title="Roman Republic">Roman Republic</a> was established <abbr title="circa">c.</abbr><span style="white-space:nowrap;"> 509 BC</span>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[26]</a></sup> when the last of the seven kings of Rome, <a href="/wiki/Lucius_Tarquinius_Superbus" title="Lucius Tarquinius Superbus">Tarquin the Proud</a>, was <a href="/wiki/Overthrow_of_the_Roman_monarchy" title="Overthrow of the Roman monarchy">deposed</a> by <a href="/wiki/Lucius_Junius_Brutus" title="Lucius Junius Brutus">Lucius Junius Brutus</a> and a system based on annually elected <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Magistrate" title="Roman Magistrate">magistrates</a> and various representative assemblies was established.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[27]</a></sup> A <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_the_Roman_Republic" title="Constitution of the Roman Republic">constitution</a> set a series of <a href="/wiki/Separation_of_powers" title="Separation of powers">checks and balances</a>, and a <a href="/wiki/Separation_of_powers" title="Separation of powers">separation of powers</a>. The most important magistrates were the two <a href="/wiki/Roman_consul" title="Roman consul">consuls</a>, who together exercised executive authority such as <i><a href="/wiki/Imperium" title="Imperium">imperium</a></i>, or military command.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAdkinsAdkins199841–42_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAdkinsAdkins199841–42-30">[28]</a></sup> The consuls had to work with the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Senate" title="Roman Senate">Senate</a>, which was initially an advisory council of the ranking nobility, or <a href="/wiki/Patrician_(ancient_Rome)" title="Patrician (ancient Rome)">patricians</a>, but grew in size and power.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[29]</a></sup>
</p><p>Other magistrates of the Republic include <a href="/wiki/Tribune" title="Tribune">tribunes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Quaestor" title="Quaestor">quaestors</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aedile" title="Aedile">aediles</a>, <a href="/wiki/Praetor" title="Praetor">praetors</a> and <a href="/wiki/Roman_censor" title="Roman censor">censors</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lacus_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-Lacus-32">[30]</a></sup> The magistracies were originally restricted to <a href="/wiki/Patrician_(ancient_Rome)" title="Patrician (ancient Rome)">patricians</a>, but were later opened to common people, or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Plebs" title="Plebs">plebeians</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[31]</a></sup> Republican voting assemblies included the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Comitia_centuriata" title="Comitia centuriata">comitia centuriata</a></i> (centuriate assembly), which voted on matters of war and peace and elected men to the most important offices, and the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Comitia_tributa" title="Comitia tributa">comitia tributa</a></i> (tribal assembly), which elected less important offices.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAdkinsAdkins199839_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAdkinsAdkins199839-34">[32]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Italy_400bC_en.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="890" data-file-width="747" decoding="async" height="357" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Italy_400bC_en.svg/300px-Italy_400bC_en.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Italy_400bC_en.svg/450px-Italy_400bC_en.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Italy_400bC_en.svg/600px-Italy_400bC_en.svg.png 2x" width="300"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Italy_400bC_en.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a> in 400 BC.</div></div></div>
<p>In the 4th century BC, Rome had come under attack by the <a href="/wiki/Gauls" title="Gauls">Gauls</a>, who now extended their power in the Italian peninsula beyond the <a href="/wiki/Po_Valley" title="Po Valley">Po Valley</a> and through Etruria. On 16 July 390 BC, a Gallic army under the leadership of tribal chieftain <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Brennus_(4th_century_BC)" title="Brennus (4th century BC)">Brennus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Allia" title="Battle of the Allia">met the Romans</a> on the banks of the Allia River ten miles north of Rome. Brennus defeated the Romans, and the Gauls marched to Rome. Most Romans had fled the city, but some barricaded themselves upon the Capitoline Hill for a last stand. The Gauls looted and burned the city, then laid siege to the Capitoline Hill. The siege lasted seven months. The Gauls then agreed to give the Romans peace in exchange for 1000 pounds of gold.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[33]</a></sup> According to later legend, the Roman supervising the weighing noticed that the Gauls were using false scales. The Romans then took up arms and defeated the Gauls. Their victorious general <a href="/wiki/Marcus_Furius_Camillus" title="Marcus Furius Camillus">Camillus</a> remarked "With iron, not with gold, Rome buys her freedom."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[34]</a></sup>
</p><p>The Romans <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_conquest_of_Italy" title="Roman conquest of Italy">gradually subdued</a> the other peoples on the Italian peninsula, including the <a href="/wiki/Etruscan_civilization" title="Etruscan civilization">Etruscans</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-haywood_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-haywood-37">[35]</a></sup> The last threat to Roman <a href="/wiki/Hegemony" title="Hegemony">hegemony</a> in Italy came when <a href="/wiki/Taranto" title="Taranto">Tarentum</a>, a major <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Greece" title="Ancient Greece">Greek</a> colony, enlisted the aid of <a href="/wiki/Pyrrhus_of_Epirus" title="Pyrrhus of Epirus">Pyrrhus of Epirus</a> in 281 BC, but this effort failed as well.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[36]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-haywood_37-1"><a href="#cite_note-haywood-37">[35]</a></sup> The Romans secured their conquests by founding <a href="/wiki/Colonies_in_antiquity" title="Colonies in antiquity">Roman colonies</a> in strategic areas, thereby establishing stable control over the region of Italy they had conquered.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-haywood_37-2"><a href="#cite_note-haywood-37">[35]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Punic_Wars">Punic Wars</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ancient_Rome&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Punic Wars">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Punic_Wars" title="Punic Wars">Punic Wars</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Roman_conquest_of_the_Iberian_Peninsula" title="Roman conquest of the Iberian Peninsula">Roman conquest of the Iberian Peninsula</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Domain_changes_during_the_Punic_Wars.gif"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="800" decoding="async" height="225" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Domain_changes_during_the_Punic_Wars.gif/300px-Domain_changes_during_the_Punic_Wars.gif" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Domain_changes_during_the_Punic_Wars.gif/450px-Domain_changes_during_the_Punic_Wars.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Domain_changes_during_the_Punic_Wars.gif/600px-Domain_changes_during_the_Punic_Wars.gif 2x" width="300"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Domain_changes_during_the_Punic_Wars.gif" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Rome and Carthage possession changes during the Punic Wars <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#ffcb90; color:black;"> </span> Carthaginian possessions</div> <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#b4d5b1; color:black;"> </span> Roman possessions</div></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:RUSSELL(1854)_p182_Siege_of_Numantia.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="986" data-file-width="1297" decoding="async" height="167" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/RUSSELL%281854%29_p182_Siege_of_Numantia.jpg/220px-RUSSELL%281854%29_p182_Siege_of_Numantia.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/RUSSELL%281854%29_p182_Siege_of_Numantia.jpg/330px-RUSSELL%281854%29_p182_Siege_of_Numantia.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/RUSSELL%281854%29_p182_Siege_of_Numantia.jpg/440px-RUSSELL%281854%29_p182_Siege_of_Numantia.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:RUSSELL(1854)_p182_Siege_of_Numantia.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Roman siege of the <a href="/wiki/Celtiberians" title="Celtiberians">Celtiberian</a> stronghold of <a href="/wiki/Numantia" title="Numantia">Numantia</a> in present north-central Spain by <a href="/wiki/Scipio_Aemilianus" title="Scipio Aemilianus">Scipio Aemilianus</a> in 133 BC<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[37]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>In the 3rd century BC Rome faced a new and formidable opponent: <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Carthage" title="Ancient Carthage">Carthage</a>. Carthage was a rich, flourishing <a href="/wiki/Phoenicia" title="Phoenicia">Phoenician</a> <a href="/wiki/City-state" title="City-state">city-state</a> that intended to dominate the Mediterranean area. The two cities were allies in the times of Pyrrhus, who was a menace to both, but with Rome's hegemony in mainland Italy and the Carthaginian <a href="/wiki/Thalassocracy" title="Thalassocracy">thalassocracy</a>, these cities became the two major powers in the Western Mediterranean and their contention over the Mediterranean led to conflict.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGoldsworthy200625–26_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGoldsworthy200625–26-40">[38]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMiles2011175–176_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMiles2011175–176-41">[39]</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/First_Punic_War" title="First Punic War">First Punic War</a> began in 264 BC, when the city of <a href="/wiki/Messina" title="Messina">Messana</a> asked for Carthage's help in their conflicts with <a href="/wiki/Hiero_II_of_Syracuse" title="Hiero II of Syracuse">Hiero II of Syracuse</a>. After the Carthaginian intercession, Messana asked Rome to expel the Carthaginians. Rome entered this war because <a href="/wiki/Syracuse,_Sicily" title="Syracuse, Sicily">Syracuse</a> and Messana were too close to the newly conquered Greek cities of Southern Italy and Carthage was now able to make an offensive through Roman territory; along with this, Rome could extend its domain over <a href="/wiki/Sicily" title="Sicily">Sicily</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[40]</a></sup>
</p><p>Although the Romans had experience in land battles, defeating this new enemy required naval battles. Carthage was a maritime power, and the Roman lack of ships and naval experience made the path to the victory a long and difficult one for the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Republic" title="Roman Republic">Roman Republic</a>. Despite this, after more than 20 years of war, Rome defeated Carthage and a peace treaty was signed. Among the reasons for the <a href="/wiki/Second_Punic_War" title="Second Punic War">Second Punic War</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[41]</a></sup> was the subsequent war reparations Carthage acquiesced to at the end of the First Punic War.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[42]</a></sup>
</p><p>Generals on both sides of the Second Punic War were brilliant planners: on the Punic side were <a href="/wiki/Hannibal" title="Hannibal">Hannibal</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hasdrubal_(Barcid)" title="Hasdrubal (Barcid)">Hasdrubal</a>; on the Roman were <a href="/wiki/Marcus_Claudius_Marcellus" title="Marcus Claudius Marcellus">Marcus Claudius Marcellus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Quintus_Fabius_Maximus_Verrucosus" title="Quintus Fabius Maximus Verrucosus">Quintus Fabius Maximus Verrucosus</a> and <a href="/wiki/Scipio_Africanus" title="Scipio Africanus">Publius Cornelius Scipio</a>. Rome fought this war simultaneously with the <a href="/wiki/First_Macedonian_War" title="First Macedonian War">First Macedonian War</a>. The war began with the audacious invasion of Hispania by Hannibal, son of <a href="/wiki/Hamilcar_Barca" title="Hamilcar Barca">Hamilcar Barca</a>, a Carthaginian general who had led operations on Sicily towards the end of the First Punic War. Hannibal rapidly marched through <a href="/wiki/Hispania" title="Hispania">Hispania</a> to the Italian <a href="/wiki/Alps" title="Alps">Alps</a>, causing panic among Rome's Italian allies. The best way found to defeat Hannibal's purpose of causing the Italians to abandon Rome was to delay the Carthaginians with a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Guerrilla" title="Guerrilla">guerrilla</a> war of attrition, a strategy propounded by Quintus Fabius Maximus, who would be nicknamed <i>Cunctator</i> ("delayer" in Latin), and whose strategy would be forever after known as <a href="/wiki/Fabian_strategy" title="Fabian strategy">Fabian</a>. Due to this, Hannibal's goal was unachieved: he could not bring enough Italian cities to revolt against Rome and replenish his diminishing army, and he thus lacked the machines and manpower to besiege Rome.
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Escipi%C3%B3n_africano.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="5021" data-file-width="3038" decoding="async" height="281" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Escipi%C3%B3n_africano.JPG/170px-Escipi%C3%B3n_africano.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Escipi%C3%B3n_africano.JPG/255px-Escipi%C3%B3n_africano.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Escipi%C3%B3n_africano.JPG/340px-Escipi%C3%B3n_africano.JPG 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Escipi%C3%B3n_africano.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Roman_portraiture" title="Roman portraiture">Roman bronze bust</a> of an unknown man, traditionally identified as <a href="/wiki/Scipio_Africanus" title="Scipio Africanus">Scipio Africanus the Elder</a> from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Naples_National_Archaeological_Museum" title="Naples National Archaeological Museum">Naples National Archaeological Museum</a> (Inv. No. 5634), <br/>dated to mid 1st century BC<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[43]</a></sup> <br/>Excavated from the <a href="/wiki/Villa_of_the_Papyri" title="Villa of the Papyri">Villa of the Papyri</a> at <a href="/wiki/Herculaneum" title="Herculaneum">Herculaneum</a> by <a href="/wiki/Karl_Jakob_Weber" title="Karl Jakob Weber">Karl Jakob Weber</a>, 1750–65<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[44]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>Still, Hannibal's invasion lasted over 16 years, ravaging Italy. Finally, when the Romans perceived the depletion of Hannibal's supplies, they sent Scipio, who had defeated Hannibal's brother Hasdrubal in modern-day Spain, to invade the unprotected Carthaginian hinterland and force Hannibal to return to defend Carthage itself. The result was the ending of the Second Punic War by the decisive <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Zama" title="Battle of Zama">Battle of Zama</a> in October 202 BC, which gave to Scipio his <a href="/wiki/Agnomen" title="Agnomen">agnomen</a> <i>Africanus</i>. At great cost, Rome had made significant gains: the conquest of Hispania by Scipio, and of Syracuse, the last Greek realm in Sicily, by Marcellus.
</p><p>More than a half century after these events, Carthage was humiliated and Rome was no more concerned about the African menace. The Republic's focus now was only to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hellenistic" title="Hellenistic">Hellenistic</a> kingdoms of Greece and <a href="/wiki/Celtiberian_Wars" title="Celtiberian Wars">revolts in Hispania</a>. However, Carthage, after having paid the war indemnity, felt that its commitments and submission to Rome had ceased, a vision not shared by the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Senate" title="Roman Senate">Roman Senate</a>. When in 151 BC <a href="/wiki/Numidia" title="Numidia">Numidia</a> invaded Carthage, Carthage asked for Roman intercession. Ambassadors were sent to Carthage, among them was <a href="/wiki/Cato_the_Elder" title="Cato the Elder">Marcus Porcius Cato</a>, who after seeing that Carthage could make a comeback and regain its importance, ended all his speeches, no matter what the subject was, by saying: "<i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ceterum_censeo_Carthaginem_esse_delendam" title="Ceterum censeo Carthaginem esse delendam">Ceterum censeo Carthaginem esse delendam</a></i>" ("Furthermore, I think that Carthage must be destroyed").
</p><p>As Carthage fought with Numidia without Roman consent, the <a href="/wiki/Third_Punic_War" title="Third Punic War">Third Punic War</a> began when Rome declared war against Carthage in 149 BC. Carthage resisted well at the first strike, with the participation of all the inhabitants of the city. However, Carthage could not withstand the attack of <a href="/wiki/Scipio_Aemilianus" title="Scipio Aemilianus">Scipio Aemilianus</a>, who entirely destroyed the city and its walls, enslaved and sold all the citizens and gained control of that region, which became the province of <a href="/wiki/Africa_(Roman_province)" title="Africa (Roman province)">Africa</a>. Thus ended the Punic War period. All these wars resulted in Rome's first overseas conquests (Sicily, Hispania and Africa) and the rise of Rome as a significant imperial power and began the end of democracy.
<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-haywood2_47-0"><a href="#cite_note-haywood2-47">[45]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[46]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Late_Republic">Late Republic</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ancient_Rome&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Late Republic">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>After defeating the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Macedon" title="Macedon">Macedonian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Seleucid_Empire" title="Seleucid Empire">Seleucid Empires</a> in the 2nd century BC, the <a href="/wiki/Roman_people" title="Roman people">Romans</a> became the dominant people of the <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_Sea" title="Mediterranean Sea">Mediterranean Sea</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[47]</a></sup> The conquest of the Hellenistic kingdoms brought the Roman and Greek cultures in closer contact and the Roman elite, once rural, became a luxurious and cosmopolitan one. At this time Rome was a consolidated empire—in the military view—and had no major enemies.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Marius_Carthage.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3908" data-file-width="2904" decoding="async" height="229" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Marius_Carthage.jpg/170px-Marius_Carthage.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Marius_Carthage.jpg/255px-Marius_Carthage.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Marius_Carthage.jpg/340px-Marius_Carthage.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Marius_Carthage.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Gaius_Marius" title="Gaius Marius">Gaius Marius</a>, a Roman general and politician who dramatically reformed the <a href="/wiki/Military_history_of_ancient_Rome" title="Military history of ancient Rome">Roman military</a></div></div></div><p>Foreign dominance led to internal strife. Senators became rich at the <a href="/wiki/Roman_province" title="Roman province">provinces</a>' expense; soldiers, who were mostly small-scale farmers, were away from home longer and could not maintain their land; and the increased reliance on foreign <a href="/wiki/Slavery_in_antiquity" title="Slavery in antiquity">slaves</a> and the growth of <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Latifundia" title="Latifundia">latifundia</a></i> reduced the availability of paid work.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[48]</a></sup>
</p><p>Income from war booty, <a href="/wiki/Mercantilism" title="Mercantilism">mercantilism</a> in the new provinces, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tax_farming" title="Tax farming">tax farming</a> created new economic opportunities for the wealthy, forming a new class of <a href="/wiki/Merchant" title="Merchant">merchants</a>, called the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Equestrian_order" title="Equestrian order">equestrians</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Liviuseques_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-Liviuseques-51">[49]</a></sup> The <i><a href="/wiki/Lex_Claudia" title="Lex Claudia">lex Claudia</a></i> forbade members of the Senate from engaging in commerce, so while the equestrians could theoretically join the Senate, they were severely restricted in political power.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Liviuseques_51-1"><a href="#cite_note-Liviuseques-51">[49]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAdkinsAdkins199838_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAdkinsAdkins199838-52">[50]</a></sup> The Senate squabbled perpetually, repeatedly blocked important <a href="/wiki/Land_reform" title="Land reform">land reforms</a> and refused to give the equestrian class a larger say in the government.
</p><p>Violent gangs of the urban unemployed, controlled by rival Senators, intimidated the electorate through violence. The situation came to a head in the late 2nd century BC under the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gracchi" title="Gracchi">Gracchi</a> brothers, a pair of <a href="/wiki/Tribune" title="Tribune">tribunes</a> who attempted to pass land reform legislation that would redistribute the major patrician landholdings among the plebeians. Both brothers were killed and the Senate passed reforms reversing the Gracchi brother's actions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[51]</a></sup> This led to the growing divide of the plebeian groups (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Populares" title="Populares">populares</a>) and equestrian classes (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Optimates" title="Optimates">optimates</a>).
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Marius_and_Sulla">Marius and Sulla</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ancient_Rome&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Marius and Sulla">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Gaius_Marius" title="Gaius Marius">Gaius Marius</a>, a <i><a href="/wiki/Novus_homo" title="Novus homo">novus homo</a></i>, who started his political career with the help of the powerful <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Metelli" title="Metelli">Metelli</a> family, soon become a leader of the Republic, holding the first of his seven consulships (an unprecedented number) in 107 BC by arguing that his former patron <a href="/wiki/Quintus_Caecilius_Metellus_Numidicus" title="Quintus Caecilius Metellus Numidicus">Quintus Caecilius Metellus Numidicus</a> was not able to defeat and capture the Numidian king <a href="/wiki/Jugurtha" title="Jugurtha">Jugurtha</a>. Marius then started his military reform: in his recruitment to fight Jugurtha, he levied the very poor (an innovation), and many landless men entered the army; this was the seed of securing loyalty of the army to the General in command.
</p><p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lucius_Cornelius_Sulla" title="Lucius Cornelius Sulla">Lucius Cornelius Sulla</a> was born into a poor family that used to be a <a href="/wiki/Patrician_(ancient_Rome)" title="Patrician (ancient Rome)">patrician</a> family. He had a good education but became poor when his father died and left none of his will. Sulla joined the theater and found many friends there, prior to becoming a general in the <a href="/wiki/Jugurthine_War" title="Jugurthine War">Jugurthine war</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[52]</a></sup>
</p><p>At this time, Marius began his quarrel with Sulla: Marius, who wanted to capture Jugurtha, asked <a href="/wiki/Bocchus_I" title="Bocchus I">Bocchus</a>, son-in-law of Jugurtha, to hand him over. As Marius failed, Sulla, a <a href="/wiki/Legatus" title="Legatus">general</a> of Marius at that time, in a dangerous enterprise, went himself to Bocchus and convinced Bocchus to hand Jugurtha over to him. This was very provocative to Marius, since many of his enemies were encouraging Sulla to oppose Marius. Despite this, Marius was elected for five consecutive consulships from 104 to 100 BC, as Rome needed a military leader to defeat the <a href="/wiki/Cimbri" title="Cimbri">Cimbri</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Teutones" title="Teutones">Teutones</a>, who were threatening Rome.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sulla_Glyptothek_Munich_309.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2508" data-file-width="1645" decoding="async" height="259" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Sulla_Glyptothek_Munich_309.jpg/170px-Sulla_Glyptothek_Munich_309.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Sulla_Glyptothek_Munich_309.jpg/255px-Sulla_Glyptothek_Munich_309.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Sulla_Glyptothek_Munich_309.jpg/340px-Sulla_Glyptothek_Munich_309.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Sulla_Glyptothek_Munich_309.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Portrait bust formerly identified as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lucius_Cornelius_Sulla" title="Lucius Cornelius Sulla">Lucius Cornelius Sulla</a></div></div></div>
<p>After Marius's retirement, Rome had a brief peace, during which the Italian <i>socii</i> ("allies" in Latin) requested Roman citizenship and voting rights. The reformist <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Marcus_Livius_Drusus_(tribune)" title="Marcus Livius Drusus (tribune)">Marcus Livius Drusus</a> supported their legal process but was assassinated, and the <i>socii</i> revolted against the Romans in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Social_War_(91-88_BC)" title="Social War (91-88 BC)">Social War</a>. At one point both consuls were killed; Marius was appointed to command the army together with <a href="/wiki/Lucius_Julius_Caesar_(consul_90_BC)" title="Lucius Julius Caesar (consul 90 BC)">Lucius Julius Caesar</a> and Sulla.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHdP-EBp760_55-0"><a href="#cite_note-WHdP-EBp760-55">[53]</a></sup>
</p><p>By the end of the Social War, Marius and Sulla were the premier military men in Rome and their partisans were in conflict, both sides jostling for power. In 88 BC, Sulla was elected for his first consulship and his first assignment was to defeat <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mithridates_VI" title="Mithridates VI">Mithridates VI</a> of <a href="/wiki/Pontus_(region)" title="Pontus (region)">Pontus</a>, whose intentions were to conquer the Eastern part of the Roman territories. However, Marius's partisans managed his installation to the military command, defying Sulla and the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Senate" title="Roman Senate">Senate</a>, and this caused Sulla's wrath. To consolidate his own power, Sulla conducted a surprising and illegal action: he marched to Rome with his legions, killing all those who showed support to Marius's cause and impaling their heads in the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Forum" title="Roman Forum">Roman Forum</a>. In the following year, 87 BC, Marius, who had fled at Sulla's march, returned to Rome while Sulla was campaigning in Greece. He seized power along with the consul <a href="/wiki/Lucius_Cornelius_Cinna" title="Lucius Cornelius Cinna">Lucius Cornelius Cinna</a> and killed the other consul, <a href="/wiki/Gnaeus_Octavius_(consul_87_BC)" title="Gnaeus Octavius (consul 87 BC)">Gnaeus Octavius</a>, achieving his seventh consulship. In an attempt to raise Sulla's anger, Marius and Cinna revenged their partisans by conducting a massacre.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHdP-EBp760_55-1"><a href="#cite_note-WHdP-EBp760-55">[53]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[54]</a></sup>
</p><p>Marius died in 86 BC, due to age and poor health, just a few months after seizing power. Cinna exercised absolute power until his death in 84 BC. After returning from his Eastern campaigns, Sulla had a free path to reestablish his own power. In 83 BC he made his <a href="/wiki/Sulla%27s_civil_war" title="Sulla's civil war">second march in Rome</a> and began a time of terror: thousands of nobles, knights and senators were executed. Sulla also held two <a href="/wiki/Roman_dictator" title="Roman dictator">dictatorships</a> and one more consulship, which began the crisis and decline of Roman Republic.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHdP-EBp760_55-2"><a href="#cite_note-WHdP-EBp760-55">[53]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Caesar_and_the_First_Triumvirate">Caesar and the First Triumvirate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ancient_Rome&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Caesar and the First Triumvirate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Landing_of_the_Romans_on_the_Coast_of_Kent.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="580" data-file-width="491" decoding="async" height="260" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Landing_of_the_Romans_on_the_Coast_of_Kent.jpg/220px-Landing_of_the_Romans_on_the_Coast_of_Kent.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Landing_of_the_Romans_on_the_Coast_of_Kent.jpg/330px-Landing_of_the_Romans_on_the_Coast_of_Kent.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Landing_of_the_Romans_on_the_Coast_of_Kent.jpg/440px-Landing_of_the_Romans_on_the_Coast_of_Kent.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Landing_of_the_Romans_on_the_Coast_of_Kent.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Landing of the Romans in <a href="/wiki/Kent" title="Kent">Kent</a>, 55 BC: Caesar with 100 ships and two legions made an opposed landing, probably near <a href="/wiki/Deal,_Kent" title="Deal, Kent">Deal</a>. After pressing a little way inland against fierce opposition and losing ships in a storm, he retired back across the <a href="/wiki/English_Channel" title="English Channel">English Channel</a> to Gaul from what was a reconnaissance in force, only to return the following year for a more serious <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Caesar%27s_invasions_of_Britain" title="Caesar's invasions of Britain">invasion</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>In the mid-1st century BC, Roman politics were restless. Political divisions in Rome became identified with two groupings, <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Populares" title="Populares">populares</a></i> (who hoped for the support of the people) and <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Optimates" title="Optimates">optimates</a></i> (the "best", who wanted to maintain exclusive aristocratic control). Sulla overthrew all populist leaders and his constitutional reforms removed powers (such as those of the <a href="/wiki/Tribune_of_the_plebs" title="Tribune of the plebs">tribune of the plebs</a>) that had supported populist approaches. Meanwhile, social and economic stresses continued to build; Rome had become a metropolis with a super-rich aristocracy, debt-ridden aspirants, and a large proletariat often of impoverished farmers. The latter groups supported the <a href="/wiki/Catiline" title="Catiline">Catilinarian conspiracy</a>—a resounding failure, since the consul <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Marcus_Tullius_Cicero" title="Marcus Tullius Cicero">Marcus Tullius Cicero</a> quickly arrested and executed the main leaders of the conspiracy.
</p><p>Onto this turbulent scene emerged <a href="/wiki/Julius_Caesar" title="Julius Caesar">Gaius Julius Caesar</a>, from an aristocratic family of limited wealth. <a href="/wiki/Julia_(wife_of_Marius)" title="Julia (wife of Marius)">His aunt Julia</a> was Marius' wife,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Plutarch_57-0"><a href="#cite_note-Plutarch-57">[55]</a></sup> and Caesar identified with the populares. To achieve power, Caesar reconciled the two most powerful men in Rome: <a href="/wiki/Marcus_Licinius_Crassus" title="Marcus Licinius Crassus">Marcus Licinius Crassus</a>, who had financed much of his earlier career, and Crassus' rival, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gnaeus_Pompeius_Magnus" title="Gnaeus Pompeius Magnus">Gnaeus Pompeius Magnus</a> (anglicized as Pompey), to whom he married <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Julia_(daughter_of_Julius_Caesar)" title="Julia (daughter of Julius Caesar)">his daughter</a>. He formed them into a new informal alliance including himself, the <a href="/wiki/First_Triumvirate" title="First Triumvirate">First Triumvirate</a> ("three men"). This satisfied the interests of all three: Crassus, the richest man in Rome, became richer and ultimately achieved high military command; Pompey exerted more influence in the Senate; and Caesar obtained the consulship and military command in <a href="/wiki/Gaul" title="Gaul">Gaul</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[56]</a></sup> So long as they could agree, the three were in effect the rulers of Rome.
</p><p>In 54 BC, Caesar's daughter, Pompey's wife, died in childbirth, unraveling one link in the alliance. In 53 BC, Crassus invaded <a href="/wiki/Parthia" title="Parthia">Parthia</a> and was killed in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Carrhae" title="Battle of Carrhae">Battle of Carrhae</a>. The Triumvirate disintegrated at Crassus' death. Crassus had acted as mediator between Caesar and Pompey, and, without him, the two generals manoeuvred against each other for power. Caesar <a href="/wiki/Gallic_Wars" title="Gallic Wars">conquered Gaul</a>, obtaining immense wealth, respect in Rome and the loyalty of battle-hardened legions. He also became a clear menace to Pompey and was loathed by many <i>optimates</i>. Confident that Caesar could be stopped by legal means, Pompey's party tried to strip Caesar of his legions, a prelude to Caesar's trial, impoverishment, and exile.
</p><p>To avoid this fate, Caesar <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Caesar%27s_Civil_War" title="Caesar's Civil War">crossed the Rubicon</a> River and invaded Rome in 49 BC. Pompey and his party fled from Italy, pursued by Caesar. The <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Pharsalus" title="Battle of Pharsalus">Battle of Pharsalus</a> was a brilliant victory for Caesar and in this and other campaigns he destroyed all of the <i>optimates'</i> leaders: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Metellus_Scipio" title="Metellus Scipio">Metellus Scipio</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cato_the_Younger" title="Cato the Younger">Cato the Younger</a>, and Pompey's son, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gnaeus_Pompeius_(son_of_Pompey_the_Great)" title="Gnaeus Pompeius (son of Pompey the Great)">Gnaeus Pompeius</a>. Pompey was murdered in Egypt in 48 BC. Caesar was now pre-eminent over Rome, attracting the bitter enmity of many aristocrats. He was granted many offices and honours. In just five years, he held four consulships, two ordinary dictatorships, and two special dictatorships: one for ten years and another for perpetuity. He was murdered in 44 BC, on the <a href="/wiki/Ides_of_March" title="Ides of March">Ides of March</a> by the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Liberatores" title="Liberatores">Liberatores</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[57]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Octavian_and_the_Second_Triumvirate">Octavian and the Second Triumvirate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ancient_Rome&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Octavian and the Second Triumvirate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:312px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Castro_Battle_of_Actium.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="900" data-file-width="1280" decoding="async" height="218" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Castro_Battle_of_Actium.jpg/310px-Castro_Battle_of_Actium.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Castro_Battle_of_Actium.jpg/465px-Castro_Battle_of_Actium.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Castro_Battle_of_Actium.jpg/620px-Castro_Battle_of_Actium.jpg 2x" width="310"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Castro_Battle_of_Actium.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i>The <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Actium" title="Battle of Actium">Battle of Actium</a></i>, by <a href="/wiki/Laureys_a_Castro" title="Laureys a Castro">Laureys a Castro</a>, painted 1672, National Maritime Museum, London</div></div></div>
<p>Caesar's assassination caused political and social turmoil in Rome; without the dictator's leadership, the city was ruled by his friend and colleague, <a href="/wiki/Mark_Antony" title="Mark Antony">Marcus Antonius</a>. Soon afterward, <a href="/wiki/Augustus" title="Augustus">Octavius</a>, whom Caesar adopted through his will, arrived in Rome. Octavian (historians regard Octavius as Octavian due to the <a href="/wiki/Roman_naming_conventions" title="Roman naming conventions">Roman naming conventions</a>) tried to align himself with the Caesarian faction. In 43 BC, along with Antony and <a href="/wiki/Marcus_Aemilius_Lepidus_(triumvir)" title="Marcus Aemilius Lepidus (triumvir)">Marcus Aemilius Lepidus</a>, Caesar's best friend,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[58]</a></sup> he legally established the <a href="/wiki/Second_Triumvirate" title="Second Triumvirate">Second Triumvirate</a>. This alliance would last for five years. Upon its formation, 130–300 senators were executed, and their property was confiscated, due to their supposed support for the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Liberatores" title="Liberatores">Liberatores</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[59]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 42 BC, the Senate <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Imperial_cult_(ancient_Rome)" title="Imperial cult (ancient Rome)">deified</a> Caesar as <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Divus_Iulius" title="Divus Iulius">Divus Iulius</a></i>; Octavian thus became <i><a href="/wiki/Divi_filius" title="Divi filius">Divi filius</a></i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[60]</a></sup> the son of the deified. In the same year, Octavian and Antony defeated both Caesar's assassins and the leaders of the <i>Liberatores</i>, <a href="/wiki/Marcus_Junius_Brutus" title="Marcus Junius Brutus">Marcus Junius Brutus</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gaius_Cassius_Longinus" title="Gaius Cassius Longinus">Gaius Cassius Longinus</a>, in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Philippi" title="Battle of Philippi">Battle of Philippi</a>. The Second Triumvirate was marked by the <a href="/wiki/Proscription" title="Proscription">proscriptions</a> of many senators and <i>equites</i>: after a revolt led by Antony's brother <a href="/wiki/Lucius_Antonius_(brother_of_Mark_Antony)" title="Lucius Antonius (brother of Mark Antony)">Lucius Antonius</a>, more than 300 senators and <i>equites</i> involved were executed on the anniversary of the <a href="/wiki/Ides_of_March" title="Ides of March">Ides of March</a>, although Lucius was spared.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[61]</a></sup> The Triumvirate proscribed several important men, including <a href="/wiki/Cicero" title="Cicero">Cicero</a>, whom Antony hated;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[62]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Quintus_Tullius_Cicero" title="Quintus Tullius Cicero">Quintus Tullius Cicero</a>, the younger brother of the orator; and <a href="/wiki/Lucius_Julius_Caesar_(consul_64_BC)" title="Lucius Julius Caesar (consul 64 BC)">Lucius Julius Caesar</a>, cousin and friend of the acclaimed general, for his support of Cicero. However, Lucius was pardoned, perhaps because his sister Julia had intervened for him.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[63]</a></sup>
</p><p>The Triumvirate divided the Empire among the triumvirs: Lepidus was given charge of <a href="/wiki/Africa_(Roman_province)" title="Africa (Roman province)">Africa</a>, Antony, the eastern provinces, and Octavian remained in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Italy_(Roman_Empire)" title="Italy (Roman Empire)">Italia</a> and controlled <a href="/wiki/Hispania" title="Hispania">Hispania</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gaul" title="Gaul">Gaul</a>. The Second Triumvirate expired in 38 BC but was renewed for five more years. However, the relationship between Octavian and Antony had deteriorated, and Lepidus was forced to retire in 36 BC after betraying Octavian in <a href="/wiki/Bellum_Siculum" title="Bellum Siculum">Sicily</a>. By the end of the Triumvirate, Antony was living in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ptolemaic_Egypt" title="Ptolemaic Egypt">Ptolemaic Egypt</a>, an independent and rich kingdom ruled by his lover, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cleopatra_VII" title="Cleopatra VII">Cleopatra VII</a>. Antony's affair with Cleopatra was seen as an act of treason, since she was queen of another country. Additionally, Antony adopted a lifestyle considered too extravagant and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hellenistic" title="Hellenistic">Hellenistic</a> for a Roman statesman.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[64]</a></sup> Following Antony's <a href="/wiki/Donations_of_Alexandria" title="Donations of Alexandria">Donations of Alexandria</a>, which <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Reign_of_Cleopatra_VII" title="Reign of Cleopatra VII">gave to Cleopatra</a> the title of "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Queen_of_Kings" title="Queen of Kings">Queen of Kings</a>", and to Antony's and Cleopatra's children the regal titles to the newly conquered Eastern territories, <a href="/wiki/War_of_Actium" title="War of Actium">war between Octavian and Antony broke out</a>. Octavian annihilated Egyptian forces in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Actium" title="Battle of Actium">Battle of Actium</a> in 31 BC. <a href="/wiki/Death_of_Cleopatra" title="Death of Cleopatra">Antony and Cleopatra committed suicide</a>. Now Egypt was conquered by the Roman Empire, and for the Romans, a new era had begun.
</p>
<h2><span id="Empire_.E2.80.93_the_Principate"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Empire_–_the_Principate">Empire – the Principate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ancient_Rome&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Empire – the Principate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Roman Empire</a></div>
<p>In 27 BC and at the age of 36, Octavian was the sole Roman leader. In that year, he took the name <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Augustus_(honorific)" title="Augustus (honorific)">Augustus</a></i>. That event is usually taken by historians as the beginning of Roman Empire—although Rome was an "imperial" state since 146 BC, when Carthage was razed by <a href="/wiki/Scipio_Aemilianus" title="Scipio Aemilianus">Scipio Aemilianus</a> and Greece was conquered by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lucius_Mummius" title="Lucius Mummius">Lucius Mummius</a>. Officially, the government was republican, but Augustus assumed absolute powers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[65]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated14_68-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated14-68">[66]</a></sup> His <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_reforms_of_Augustus" title="Constitutional reforms of Augustus">reform of the government</a> brought about a two-century period colloquially referred to by Romans as the <a href="/wiki/Pax_Romana" title="Pax Romana">Pax Romana</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Julio-Claudian_dynasty">Julio-Claudian dynasty</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ancient_Rome&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Julio-Claudian dynasty">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Julio-Claudian_dynasty" title="Julio-Claudian dynasty">Julio-Claudian dynasty</a> was established by <a href="/wiki/Augustus" title="Augustus">Augustus</a>. The emperors of this dynasty were Augustus, <a href="/wiki/Tiberius" title="Tiberius">Tiberius</a>, <a href="/wiki/Caligula" title="Caligula">Caligula</a>, <a href="/wiki/Claudius" title="Claudius">Claudius</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nero" title="Nero">Nero</a>. The dynasty is so called due to the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gens_Julia" title="Gens Julia">gens Julia</a></i>, family of Augustus, and the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gens_Claudia" title="Gens Claudia">gens Claudia</a></i>, family of Tiberius. The Julio-Claudians started the destruction of republican values, but on the other hand, they boosted Rome's status as the central power in the Mediterranean region.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[67]</a></sup> While Caligula and Nero are usually remembered in popular culture as dysfunctional emperors, Augustus and Claudius are remembered as emperors who were successful in politics and the military. This dynasty instituted imperial tradition in Rome<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[68]</a></sup> and frustrated any attempt to reestablish a Republic.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[69]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Augustus">Augustus</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ancient_Rome&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Augustus">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Statue-Augustus.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2250" data-file-width="1500" decoding="async" height="255" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Statue-Augustus.jpg/170px-Statue-Augustus.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Statue-Augustus.jpg/255px-Statue-Augustus.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Statue-Augustus.jpg/340px-Statue-Augustus.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Statue-Augustus.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Augustus_of_Prima_Porta" title="Augustus of Prima Porta">Augustus of Prima Porta</a>, 1st century AD, depicting <a href="/wiki/Augustus" title="Augustus">Augustus</a>, the first <a href="/wiki/Roman_emperor" title="Roman emperor">Roman emperor</a></div></div></div>
